25:T3cf3,<entryFree id="n402" key="أَخٌ" type="main">     
                  <form>       
                     <orth orig="" extent="full" lang="ar">أَخٌ</orth>
                     <orth extent="full" lang="ar">ذ</orth>
                  </form>, (S, Msb, K,) originally <foreign lang="ar">أَخَوٌ</foreign>, (Kh, S, Msb,) as is shown by the first of its dual forms mentioned below, and by its having a pl. like <foreign lang="ar">آبَآءٍ</foreign>, (S,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَخٌّ</foreign>, (K,) with the second letter doubled to compensate for the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign> suppressed, as is the case in <foreign lang="ar">أَبٌّ</foreign>, (TA,) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n402-1" target="أَخًا" n="1" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n403"/></foreign>, [like <foreign lang="ar">أَبًا</foreign>,] and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n402-2" target="أَخُو" n="2" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n405"/></foreign>, (IAar, K, TA, [the last, with the article prefixed to it, erroneously written in the CK <foreign lang="ar">الاُخُوٌّ</foreign>,]) and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n402-3" target="أَخْوٌ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n404"/></foreign>, like <foreign lang="ar">دَلْوٌ</foreign>, (Kr, K,) a well-known term of relationship, (K, TA,) i. e. <hi rend="ital">A brother; the son of one's father and mother, or of either of them:</hi> and also applied to <hi rend="ital">a foster-brother:</hi> (TA:) and <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical> <hi rend="ital">a friend; and a companion, an associate, or a fellow:</hi> (K:) derived from <foreign lang="ar">آخِيَّةٌ</foreign> [q. v.]; as though one <foreign lang="ar">أَخ</foreign> were tied and attached to another like as the horse is tied to the <foreign lang="ar">آخيّة</foreign>: (Har p. 42 :) or, accord. to some of the grammarians, it is from <foreign lang="ar">وَخَى</foreign> meaning <foreign lang="ar">قَصَدَ</foreign>; because the <foreign lang="ar">أَخ</foreign> has the same aim, endeavour, or desire, as his <foreign lang="ar">أَخ</foreign>: (TA:) when <foreign lang="ar">أَخ</foreign> is prefixed to another noun, its final vowel is prolonged: (Kh:) you say, <foreign lang="ar">هذَا أَخُوكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">This is thy brother,</hi> &amp;c.], and <foreign lang="ar">مَرَرْتُ بِأَخِيكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I passed by thy brother,</hi> &amp;c.], and <foreign lang="ar">رَأَيْتُ أَخَاكَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I saw thy brother,</hi> &amp;c.] : (S: [in which it is also asserted that one does not say <foreign lang="ar">أَخُو</foreign> without prefixing it to another noun; but this is inconsistent with the assertion of IAar and F, that <foreign lang="ar">الأَخُو</foreign> is a syn. of <foreign lang="ar">الأَخُ</foreign>:]) the dual is <foreign lang="ar">أَخَوَانِ</foreign>, (S, Msb, Kur xlix. 10, Ham p. 434,) or <foreign lang="ar">أَخْوَانِ</foreign>, with the <foreign lang="ar">خ</foreign> quiescent, (TA, [but this I have found nowhere else,]) and some of the Arabs say <foreign lang="ar">أَخَانِ</foreign>, (S, Msb,) and Kr mentions <foreign lang="ar">أَخُوَانِ</foreign>, with damm to the <foreign lang="ar">خ</foreign>, said by IB to occur in poetry, and held by ISd to be dual of <foreign lang="ar">أَخُو</foreign>, with damm to the <foreign lang="ar">خ</foreign>: (TA:) the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">إِخْوَةٌ</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">إِخْوَانٌ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K, &amp;c.,) the former generally applied to <hi rend="ital">brothers,</hi> and the latter to <hi rend="ital">friends</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">the like</hi>], (T, S,*) but not always, as in the Kur xlix. 10, where the former does not denote relationship, and in xxiv. 60 of the same, where the latter does denote relationship, (T, TA,) and sometimes the former is applied to a [single] man, as in the Kur iv. 12, (S,) and <foreign lang="ar">أُخْوَةٌ</foreign>, (Fr, S, Msb, K, [in the CK <foreign lang="ar">اَخْوَةٌ</foreign>,]) or this is a quasi-pl. n., (Sb, TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">أُخْوَانٌ</foreign>, (Kr, Msb, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">آخَآءٌ</foreign>, (S, K,) like <foreign lang="ar">آبَآءٌ</foreign>, (S,) and <foreign lang="ar">أُخُوٌّ</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">أُخُوَّةٌ</foreign>, (ISd, K,) the last mentioned by Lh, and thought by ISd to be formed from the next preceding by the addition of <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign> characterizing the pl. as fem., (TA,) and <foreign lang="ar">أَخُونَ</foreign>, (S, Msb, K,) and <foreign lang="ar">اخاوون</foreign>. (Msb: [there written without any syll. signs, and I have not found it elsewhere.]) The fem. of <foreign lang="ar">أَخٌ</foreign> is   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n402-4" target="أُخْتٌ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar" select="n345"/></foreign> [meaning <hi rend="ital">A sister:</hi> and <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">a female friend,</hi> &amp;c.]: (S, Msb, K, &amp;c. :) written with damm to show that the letter which has gone from it is <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign>; (S;) the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> being a substitute for the <foreign lang="ar">و</foreign>; (TA;) not to denote the fem. gender, (K, TA,) because the letter next before it is quiescent: this is the opinion of Sb, and [accord. to SM] it is the correct opinion: for Sb says that if you were to use it as a proper name of a man, you would make it perfectly decl.; and if the <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> were to denote the fem. gender, the name would not be perfectly decl.; though in one place he incidentally says that it is the sign of the fem. gender, through inadvertence: Kh, however, says that its <foreign lang="ar">ت</foreign> is [originally] <foreign lang="ar">ه</foreign> [meaning <foreign lang="ar">ة</foreign>]: and Lth, that <foreign lang="ar">أُخْتٌ</foreign> is originally <foreign lang="ar">أَخَةٌ</foreign>: and some say that it is originally <foreign lang="ar">أَخْوَةٌ</foreign>: (TA:) the dual. is <foreign lang="ar">أُخْتَانِ</foreign>: (Kh:) and the pl. is <foreign lang="ar">أَخَوَاتٌ</foreign>. (Kh, S, Msb, K.) The saying <foreign lang="ar">لَا أَخَالَكَ بِفُلَانٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Thou hast no brother,</hi> or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical> <hi rend="ital">friend, in such a one</hi>] means <foreign lang="ar">لَيْسَ لَكَ بِأَخٍ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">such a one is not a brother,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">friend, to thee</hi>]. (S, K.) It is said in a prov., <foreign lang="ar">مَنْ لَكَ بِأَخِيكَ كُلِّهِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Who will be responsible to thee for thy brother,</hi> or <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">thy friend, altogether?</hi> i. e., for his always acting to thee as a brother, or friend]. (JK.) And in another, <foreign lang="ar">رُبَّ أَخٍ لَكَ لَمْ تَلِدْهُ أُمُّكَ</foreign> [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">There is many a brother to thee whom thy mother has not brought forth</hi>]. (TA.) And in another, <foreign lang="ar">أَخُوكَ أَمِ الذَّئْبُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Is it thy brother,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the wolf?</hi>]; said in suspecting a thing: as also <foreign lang="ar">أَخُوكَ أَمِ اللَّيْلُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Is it thy brother, or is it the night</hi> that deceives thee?]. (Har p. 554.) And another saying is, <foreign lang="ar">الرُّمْحُ أَخُوكَ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">وَرُبَّمَا خَانَكَ</foreign> [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical> <hi rend="ital">The spear is thy brother, but sometimes, or often, it is unfaithful to thee</hi>]. (TA.)          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  Ibn-'Arafeh says that when <foreign lang="ar">أُخُوَّةٌ</foreign> does not relate to birth, it means conformity, or similarity; and combination, agreement, or unison, in action: hence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">هذَا الثَّوْبُ أَخُو هذَا</foreign> [<assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical> <hi rend="ital">This garment, or piece of cloth, is the like, or fellow, of this</hi>] : and hence the saying in the Kur [xvii. 29], <foreign lang="ar">كَانُوا إِخْوَانَ الشَّيَاطِينِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">They are the likes, or fellows, of the devils:</hi> and in the same [xliii. 47],   
      <foreign lang="ar">إِلَّا هِىَ أَكْبَرُ مِنْ <ref cref="n402-5" target="أُخْتِهَا" n="5" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">But it was greater than its like, or fellow;</hi> i. e., than what was like to it in truth &amp;c. (TA.) It is said in a trad., <foreign lang="ar">النَّوْمُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">أَخُ المَوْتِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Sleep is the like of death</hi>]. (El-Jámi' es-Sagheer.) One says also, <foreign lang="ar">لَقِىَ فُلَانٌ أَخَا المَوْتِ</foreign> <assumedtropical>(assumed tropical:)</assumedtropical>  <hi rend="ital">Such a one met with the like of death.</hi> (Msb, TA.)
